  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5bc0af46-d04b-4410-95cb-30445650af9d'

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3755548462072152624">Classic hardback edition of this fascinating collection of stories, featuring Tolkien’s own painting of the dragon Glaurung on the cover, which continues the tales of The Hobbit, The Lord of the Rings and The Silmarillion and contains an alternative version of The Children of Hurin.<br/><br/>Unfinished Tales is a collection of narratives ranging in time from the Elder Days of Middle</span>
  <span id="freeText3755548462072152624" style="display:none">Classic hardback edition of this fascinating collection of stories, featuring Tolkien’s own painting of the dragon Glaurung on the cover, which continues the tales of The Hobbit, The Lord of the Rings and The Silmarillion and contains an alternative version of The Children of Hurin.<br /><br />Unfinished Tales is a collection of narratives ranging in time from the Elder Days of Middle-earth to the end of the War of the Ring, and provides those who have read The Lord of the Rings with a whole collection of background and new stories from the twentieth century’s most acclaimed popular author.<br /><br />The book concentrates on the realm of Middle-earth and comprises such elements as Gandalf’s lively account of how it was that he came to send the Dwarves to the celebrated party at Bag-End, the emergence of the sea-god Ulmo before the eyes of Tuor on the coast of Beleriand, and an exact description of the military organization of the Riders of Rohan.<br /><br />Unfinished Tales also contains the only story about the long ages of Numenor before its downfall, and all that is known about such matters as the Five Wizards, the Palantiri and the legend of Amroth. The tales were collated and edited by JRR Tolkien’s son and literary heir, Christopher Tolkien, who provides a short commentary on each story, helping the reader to fill in the gaps and put each story into the context of the rest of his father’s writings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3755548462072152624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/770462-my-friends-i-have-on-my-shelf-the-story">My friends, I have on my shelf The story of Kullervo, The silmarillion, The children of Húrin, The hobbit, the trilogy of The lord of the rings and Unfinished tales of Númenor and Middle-Earth. In what order should I read them? Am I missing any book in the series?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_770462'><a id="like_count_community_question_770462" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/770462?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F7329.Unfinished_Tales_of_N_menor_and_Middle_Earth">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/46131582-michael-galdamez"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1468780624i/46131582._UX100_CR0,2,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/46131582-michael-galdamez">Michael Galdamez</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I must say I'm impressed with your collection; my suggested reading order would be:<br/><br/>1. The Hobbit (A good introductory to Tolkien & Middle Earth)<br/>2. The<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I must say I'm impressed with your collection; my suggested reading order would be:<br /><br />1. The Hobbit (A good introductory to Tolkien &amp; Middle Earth)<br />2. The Lord of the Rings Trilogy (direct sequel to The Hobbit)<br />3. The Silmarillion (mass of background stories)<br />4. Unfinished Tales (further stories)<br />5. The Children of Hurin (a fuller telling of a story from The Silmarillion)<br />6. The Story of Kullervo (an old story by Tolkien, only recently published)<br /><br />There are in fact more Middle Earth books by Tolkien out there, but they would probably be the toughest to follow of all his books. So I guess I will add:<br /><br />7. The History of Middle Earth Series (12 Books) <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/45924-the-history-of-middle-earth">https://www.goodreads.com/series/4592...</a><br /><br />Hope this helps!<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div class='communityQuestionAndAnswer'>
<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1338060-how-much-difference-is-there-between-this">How much difference is there between this book and the tales of Númenor and Middle-Earth in the Silmarillion? Is it a fuller account of those stories or something different entirely?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1338060'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F7329.Unfinished_Tales_of_N_menor_and_Middle_Earth">like</a></span>

</li>

<a href="/questions/1338060-how-much-difference-is-there-between-this">2 years ago</a>
</li>

<a href="/questions/1338060-how-much-difference-is-there-between-this">Add your answer</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/83473524-caleb-jore"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1602716898i/83473524._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/83473524-caleb-jore">Caleb Jore</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Unfinished Tales presents a lot of old manuscripts in all three main ages of Middle-earth that Tolkien never published, largely due to the reason that<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Unfinished Tales presents a lot of old manuscripts in all three main ages of Middle-earth that Tolkien never published, largely due to the reason that a lot of them are indeed unfinished. Examples include a fuller account of Tuor's journey to Gondolin, a description of the island of Númenor, and a manuscript concerning the history of Gondor and Rohan. If you enjoyed the Silmarillion, you would probably enjoy this.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_803543779" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/803543779" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/803543779?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789643343873" href="/book/show/18911912">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=epic">epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=european">european</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=literature">literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=20th-century">20th-century</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer803543779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2488800515430513204">Unfinished Tales of Númenor and Middle-Earth, J.R.R. Tolkien<br/><br/>Unfinished Tales of Númenor and Middle-earth is a collection of stories and essays by J. R. R. Tolkien that were never completed during his lifetime, but were edited by his son Christopher Tolkien and published in 1980. Many of the tales within are retold in The Silmarillion, albeit in modified forms; the work also contains a summary of the events of The Lord of the Rings told from a less personal perspective.<br/><br/>Contents:<br/>Part One: The Firs</span>
  <span id="freeText2488800515430513204" style="display:none">Unfinished Tales of Númenor and Middle-Earth, J.R.R. Tolkien<br /><br />Unfinished Tales of Númenor and Middle-earth is a collection of stories and essays by J. R. R. Tolkien that were never completed during his lifetime, but were edited by his son Christopher Tolkien and published in 1980. Many of the tales within are retold in The Silmarillion, albeit in modified forms; the work also contains a summary of the events of The Lord of the Rings told from a less personal perspective.<br /><br />Contents:<br />Part One: The First Age: Of Tuor and his Coming to Gondolin; Narn i Hîn Húrin (The Tale of the Children of Húrin).<br /><br />Part Two: The Second Age: A Description of the Island of Númenor; Aldarion and Erendis: The Mariner's Wife; The Line of Elros: Kings of Númenor; The History of the Galadriel and Celeborn the great.<br /><br />Part Three: The Third Age: The Disaster of the Gladden Fields; Cirion and Eorl and the Friendship of Gondor and Rohan; The Quest of Erebor; The Hunt for the Ring; The Battles of the Fords of Isen.<br />Part Four: The Drúedain; The Istari; The Palantíri.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز بیست و هشتم ماه دسامبر سال 2013میلادی <br /><br />عنوان: قصه‌های ناتمام نومه‌ نور و سرزمین میانه - دوران دوم؛ نویسنده جان رونالد روئل (جی.آر.آر) تالکین؛ به کوشش کریستوفر تالکین؛ مترجم رضا علیزاده؛ تهران، روزنه، 1392؛ در 216ص؛ شابک 9789643343873؛ چاپ دوم 1393؛ موضوع داستانهای نویسندگان بریتانیایی - سده 20م<br /><br />کتاب شامل چهار بخش اصلی است که هر کدام از آنها چندین داستان را در بردارند؛ که دنباله ی هر کدام از آنها، در انبوهی از یادداشتهای تکمیلی نویسنده آمده است؛ که نقاط تاریک را روشن میسازند؛ اما به گویش خود «کریستوفر» به دلیل پراکندگیهای بسیار، در دست نوشته ها، خلاءهای داستان همچنان باقی میمانند و «کریستوفر» نیز صرفا به گمانه زنی بسنده میکند<br /><br />بخش اول: بخش اول داستان «دوران اول» است. دو داستان: «تور و آمدن او به گوندولین»، و «نارن ای هین هورین» را در بر دارد. داستان اول به زندگی «تور» فرزند «هور» میپردازد. از کودکی او که میگوید در میان شرقیها گذشت، تا تقدیر بلندش که از جانب «اولمو»، خداوندگار آبها به سوی شهر پنهان «گوندولین» روان میشود، تا به شاه «تورگون» هشدار دهد. او آنجا شیفته ی «ایدریل» دختر «تورگون» میشود و برق دو درخت را در چشمان دختر میبیند. عشق آنها فراتر از نام و نژاد آنها میرود، و با یکدیگر پیوند زناشویی میبندند؛ این ازدواج، «مایگلین» خواهر زاده پادشاه را، خوش نمیآید، و به دنبال تنفرش از «تور» و از آنسو پیشرویها و پیروزیهای متعدد «مورگوت»، شهر پنهان «گوندولین» به سوی فرجام خویش گام برمیدارد، و ماجراهای اندوهباری را تجربه میکند؛ از بین این تاریکیهاست که نوری میدرخشد و آن تواناترین دریانورد ترانه ها از مهلکه نجات پیدا میکند<br /><br />بخش دوم: این بخش، روایتگر دوران دوم سرزمین میانه است. و شامل داستانهای: «وصف جزیره نومه نور»، داستان «آلداریون و ارندیس»، «دودمان الروس: شاهان نومه نور» و «سرگذشت گالادریل و کله بورن» و در باب «آمروت شاه لورین» است؛ این داستانها رخدادهای دوران دوم هستند و بیشتر درباره ی «نومه نور» است؛ جزیره ای که به شاهان آدمیان داده میشد تا در آن سکونت کنند؛ «آلداریون» و «ارندیس» داستان عشقی است، که تبدیل به نفرت میگردد. و پس از آن رخدادهای مربوط به هر کدام از شاهان بررسی میشود؛ سرگذشت «گالادریل» و «کله بورن»، و در باب «آمروت» شاه «لورین» داستانی در سرزمین میانه است، که در این کتاب آمده است<br /><br />بخش سوم: در این بخش داستانهایی از دوران سوم را، که با جنگ حلقه رابطه دارند، میخوانیم. داستانهایی همچون «مصیبت دشتهای گلادن»، «گیریون و ائورل و دوستی گوندور و روهان»، داستان «پویش اره بور»، «شکار حلقه»، و «جنگهای گدار آیزن» را در بر دارد؛ در داستان نخست از افسانه ی مرگ «ایسیلدور» میخوانیم، داستانی که روایتگر حمله ی «اورک»ها به «ایسیلدور»، در «دشتهای گلادن» است، که طی آن «ایسیلدور» کشته میشود، و حلقه در «آندوین» بزرگ غرق میشود؛ و مدتی طولانی در آنجا پنهان میماند؛ سپس از اتحاد «گیریون» و «ائورل»، و شکلگیری قلمرو «روهان»، و روابط دوستانه آنها با «گوندور» میخوانیم، چیزیکه چکیده ای از آن، در پیوستهای ارباب حلقه ها منتشر شده است؛<br /><br /> داستان «پویش اره بور» که در دهه 1950میلادی، توسط «تالکین» برای نخستین بار به رشته تحریر درآمد، قرار بود ابتدا بخشی از کتاب «ارباب حلقه ها» باشد، اما تالکین نظر خود را دیگر کرد، و تنها بخش کوتاهی از آنرا در پیوستها آورد؛ دو نسخه از داستان موجود است، یکی از زبان «فرودو بگینز» است، و دیگری که گمان میرود اصیلتر باشد روایت «گندالف سپید» است، از سفرشان به «اره بور»، که برای «فرودو بگینز»، در «میناس تی ریت»، پس از تاجگذاری شاه «اله سار»، میگوید؛ در فصل «شکار حلقه»، با جزئیات بیشتری از «شورای الروند»، و نیز سرنوشت «گولوم»، پس از زندانی شدن در «موردور»؛ و در آخرین بخش، تحت عنوان «جنگهای گدر آیزن»، با بخشی از داستان نبرد حلقه آشنا میشویم، که کمتر به آن پرداخته شده است؛ این داستان روایتگر کشته شدن «تئودرد» پسر شاه «تئودن»، طی جنگهایی است که در سواحل رود «آیزن»، پیش از رسیدن «گندالف»، و «آراگورن»، و «لگولاس»، و «گیملی»، به «ادوراس» رخ داد. نبردی که راه را برای تجاوز به «شاخ آواز» هموار کرد<br /><br />بخش چهارم: سه فصل «دروادان»، «ایستاری» و «پلانتیری» است؛ در فصل نخست تاریخ نژاد «دروادان» در دوران اول در «بلریاند» بعنوان عضوی از قوم «هالادین» میآید. طی دوران دوم بخشی در نومه نور ساکن میشوند، و بخشی به «آندراست»، در غرب «گوندور» میآیند، و نیز در دوران سوم به «روهیریم ها» در نبرد «پله نور» یاری کرده، و آنها را از مسیری امنتر و سریعتر راهنمایی کردند. در ارباب حلقه ها این ماجرا آمده است؛ در فصل دوم «ایستاری» با پنج جادوگری آشنا میشویم که به سرزمین میانه فرستاده شدند؛ و در فصل سوم هر آنچه لازم است درباره سنگهای «پلانتیر» بدانیم آمده است؛ ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="2488800515430513204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_26942453" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26942453" />
    <a title="Terry " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1262683-terry"><img alt="Terry " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316628758p2/1262683.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/26942453?book_show_action=true">Jul 11, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Terry " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Terry " href="/user/show/1262683-terry">Terry </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780395299173" href="/book/show/77674.Unfinished_Tales_of_N_menor_and_Middle_earth">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Tolkien fans, not Richard</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1262683-terry?shelf=tolkien">tolkien</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1262683-terry?shelf=that-northern-thing">that-northern-thing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1262683-terry?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer26942453" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14971160447945106833">This is the first work that showed us how Tolkien's obsessive perfectionism was a double-edged sword. On the one hand it gave us the wonderfully deep world and implied distances of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_' title='The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lord of the Rings</a>; and on the other hand it left us with a jumble of tales in various states of revision and development that had to be compiled by Tolkien's son Christopher into some form as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7332.The_Silmarillion' title='The Silmarillion by J.R.R. Tolkien' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Silmarillion</a>...a jumble of tales that, if they had been finished, would have given us a truly staggering body of work. </span>
  <span id="freeText14971160447945106833" style="display:none">This is the first work that showed us how Tolkien's obsessive perfectionism was a double-edged sword. On the one hand it gave us the wonderfully deep world and implied distances of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_" title="The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a>; and on the other hand it left us with a jumble of tales in various states of revision and development that had to be compiled by Tolkien's son Christopher into some form as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7332.The_Silmarillion" title="The Silmarillion by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Silmarillion</a>...a jumble of tales that, if they had been finished, would have given us a truly staggering body of work. Just reading the fragment that makes up the entirety of "Of Tuor and his Coming to Gondolin" makes me weep for what might have been. Given the chance to expand even half of the partial tales from _The Silmarillion_ into something equating the full treatment of the LotR would have been a wonder indeed. <br /><br />Even given the incomplete nature of the works herein, the reader is greatly repaid the effort of reading them even though many tantalizing questions are left unanswered. We get perhaps the only significant view of the land of Numenor in the Second Age; intriguing glimpses into the nature of the Istari, the Woodwoses, and the Palantiri; and expansions on the background of the Third Age and the events that led up to both <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5907.The_Hobbit__Middle_earth_Universe_" title="The Hobbit (Middle-earth Universe) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hobbit</a> and the LotR. <br /><br />A really amazing work and enjoyable read if you're a die-hard Tolkien fan.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14971160447945106833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2933190901?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bradley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bradley" href="/user/show/4213258-bradley">Bradley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 004823084" href="/book/show/43809420-unfinished-tales">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2019-shelf">2019-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=worldbuilding-sf">worldbuilding-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2933190901" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1409419097196441595">Out of all the posthumously published works of Tolkien, and this being the primary right after the Silmarillion, I have to admit it is the most interesting. We do get more expanded treatments of some of these tales in subsequent books, but all in all, the narrative structure of this tome is quite pleasing.<br/><br/>Why? It's written as actual stories. Not just excerpts, or not only just as excerpts, but as full-fledged stories in themselves, complete with all the storytelling conventions we are used to. <br/><br/>T</span>
  <span id="freeText1409419097196441595" style="display:none">Out of all the posthumously published works of Tolkien, and this being the primary right after the Silmarillion, I have to admit it is the most interesting. We do get more expanded treatments of some of these tales in subsequent books, but all in all, the narrative structure of this tome is quite pleasing.<br /><br />Why? It's written as actual stories. Not just excerpts, or not only just as excerpts, but as full-fledged stories in themselves, complete with all the storytelling conventions we are used to. <br /><br />That is to say, it doesn't read super quick like Silmarillion, but full of detail and meat like LotR. I appreciated that little detail. :) <br /><br />Of personal interest and joy, I absolutely loved the way this filled in so many of the blanks within the LotR stories, giving a much more detailed history of the Ring Wraiths, their creation, the Palantirs, the Maiar, (including such personages as Gandalf, Saruman, AND Sauron), the full histories of the Rohirrim, Gondor, Numenor, and EVEN the Wild Men!<br /><br />There's a lot that was left out of the Silmarillion, and THIS HAS IT.<br /><br />I'm not saying some parts could be classified in the OTHER category, such as the extended appendix at the end of LotR, only more so. Or the full damn concordance including an index of all terms, proper names and places with references to their original first-mentions. I.E., Silmarillion or LotR.<br /><br />This work is an awfully necessary addition for any would-be scholar of Arda. I can't say if it beats the FULL <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15351.The_Return_of_the_Shadow_The_History_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings__Part_One__The_History_of_Middle_Earth___6_" title="The Return of the Shadow The History of The Lord of the Rings, Part One (The History of Middle-Earth, #6) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Return of the Shadow: The History of The Lord of the Rings, Part One</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/77682.The_Treason_of_Isengard_The_History_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings__Part_Two__The_History_of_Middle_Earth___7_" title="The Treason of Isengard The History of The Lord of the Rings, Part Two (The History of Middle-Earth, #7) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Treason of Isengard: The History of The Lord of the Rings, Part Two</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15279.The_War_of_the_Ring__The_History_of_Middle_Earth___8_" title="The War of the Ring (The History of Middle-Earth, #8) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The War of the Ring</a>, or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23600.Sauron_Defeated_The_History_of_The_Lord_of_the_Rings__Part_Four__The_History_of_Middle_Earth___9_" title="Sauron Defeated The History of The Lord of the Rings, Part Four (The History of Middle-Earth, #9) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">Sauron Defeated: The History of The Lord of the Rings, Part Four</a> scholarly works, but for my poor, lazy-reading self, Unfinished Tales does a FINE job. :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1409419097196441595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2090121407" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2090121407" />
    <a title="leynes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45198798-leynes"><img alt="leynes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593512704p2/45198798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2090121407?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="leynes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="leynes" href="/user/show/45198798-leynes">leynes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/20206736-unfinished-tales-of-n-menor-and-middle-earth">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2090121407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14284655882772633714">I am fairly new to Tolkien as I have only gotten into his work at the end of 2015 by reading, and after some initial problems, loving <i>The Hobbit</i>. I buddy-read <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> over the course of 2016 and was quite overwhelmed with Tolkien’s dense writing style and complex world building; there were too many names of people, places and events to remember, I felt inept. Nonetheless, I admired his work and marvelled at his craft. I was especially enamoured by Tolkien’s linguistic interest and </span>
  <span id="freeText14284655882772633714" style="display:none">I am fairly new to Tolkien as I have only gotten into his work at the end of 2015 by reading, and after some initial problems, loving <i>The Hobbit</i>. I buddy-read <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> over the course of 2016 and was quite overwhelmed with Tolkien’s dense writing style and complex world building; there were too many names of people, places and events to remember, I felt inept. Nonetheless, I admired his work and marvelled at his craft. I was especially enamoured by Tolkien’s linguistic interest and his rational for his invented languages and names. <br /><br />In September 2016, I read <i>The Silmarillion</i>—that was the time I became totally electrified. <i>The Silmarillion</i> is still my absolute favorite work of his, even though it was just as overwhelming in regards to being exposed to all sorts of different people and their backstories, the tales, however, had a certain charm and brilliancy to them, I grew to love so many characters (Fëanor, Túrin Turambar and Lúthien), I needed to know more about them. That’s why I decided to jump into <i>The Children of Húrin</i> in April 2017. Upon finishing it, I cried and cried. Tolkien showed that he cannot only write epic high fantasy well, but also the most heart-shattering tragedies. Húrin and Morwen deserved better! <br /><br />In the second half of 2017 I got into his works that aren’t related to Middle-Earth: <i>Tales from the Perilous Realm</i> and <i>Roverandom</i>. These reads solidified Tolkien as one of my absolute favorite authors. No matter which endeavour this man took upon, he handled it with great care and detail. The whimsical nature of these stories reminded me of <i>The Hobbit</i>, and the long journey I had personally made alongside Tolkien and his work. <br /><br />In April 2018, Christmas and winter long past us, I read <i>Letters from Father Christmas</i> because why the heck not? It was the second time I bawled my eyes out reading his work. It is by far his most personal work (naturally, given its nonfictional nature); to glimpse at the man behind his writing—to see the kind of father he was—was fascinating and warmed my heart. His love, not only for his children but for storytelling, is so apparent throughout all of these Christmas letters. <br /><br />And this leads us, finally, to my read of his <i>Unfinished Tales</i>. I bough it almost a year ago but was too intimidated by it, having just read and loved <i>The Silmarillion</i>, to pick it up immediately. This week prove to be the perfect time to take upon this new adventure. Exploring the world of Númenor and Middle-Earth never gets old.<br /><br />Tolkien’s <i>Unfinished Tales</i> weren’t difficult to read at all. They are definitely not for newbies and people unfamiliar with his work, but if you have read <i>The Silmarillion</i>, you should be fine. It provides more detailed information about characters, events and places mentioned only briefly in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>. Versions of such tales include the origins of Gandalf and the other Istari, the death of Isildur and the loss of the One Ring in the Gladden Fields, and the founding of the kingdom of Rohan.<br /><br />My favourite tales were definitely "Of Tuor and his Coming to Gondolin", "Narn i Hîn Húrin", "Aldarion and Erendis: The Mariner's Wife" and "The Quest of Erebor". The reason for that is probably the fact that these were the most complete. These narratives were very endearing, suspenseful and well-written. The notes and appendices definitely heightened my understanding of them and helped me expand my knowledge of Middle-Earth. <br /><br />I thought it was very clever of Christopher Tolkien to put all of the tales and essays in chronological order, the first three parts aligning with the timeline of Arda by being split into the three ages of the world. The fourth part was a collection of short essays concerning the Drúedain, the Istari and the Palantíri. <br /><br />Of course, it is kind of unsatisfying (and in some places even frustrating) that the tales and essays are incomplete and sometimes even contradictory, e.g. "Of Tuor and his Coming to Gondolin" cuts off at the most interesting part: when Tuor eventually reached Gondolin and was admitted by Turgon. What happened after that, i.e. the fact that Turgon did not hearken the council of Ulmo, and the ensuing fall of Gondolin, is, unfortunately, not included. Nonetheless, I think that Christopher Tolkien did a fantastic job of curating his father’s writings and putting them into an intelligent form and order. <br /><br />Reading <i>Unfinished Tales</i> made me even more curious about Middle-Earth and what lay beyond, especially the First Age is of great interest to me. I’m still trying to figure out what to think of Galadriel, I want to know more about the downfall of Númenor and Gondolin … I am consoled only by the fact that <i>Beren and Lúthien</i> and <i>The Fall of Gondolin</i> have yet to be read by me. As soon as they’re available in my preferred editions I shall devour them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14284655882772633714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6386645119726711589" style="display:none">If you're into stuff like this, <a href="https://manuelaantao.blogspot.com/1980/10/numenor-unfinished-tales-by-j-r-r.html" rel="nofollow noopener">you can read the full review.</a><br /><br /><br /><br />Numenor: Unfinished Tales" by J. R. R. Tolkien<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />(Original Review, 1980-10-13)<br /><br /><br />The new Tolkien book is out.     <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_508612554" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/508612554" />
    <a title="Joseph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5004971-joseph"><img alt="Joseph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523632271p2/5004971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/508612554?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joseph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joseph" href="/user/show/5004971-joseph">Joseph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer508612554" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9197812322650052214">The name says it all -- these are stories primarily of the First and Second Age of Middle-earth that had never quite reached completion, even in draft form; some predate the writing of Lord of the Rings by decades but most come after, and the book includes some of Tolkien's last writings about Middle-earth. The stories are presented by his son Christopher who, presumably, selected the pieces that were nearest to completion and likeliest to be of interest to Middle-earth aficionados. The pieces a</span>
  <span id="freeText9197812322650052214" style="display:none">The name says it all -- these are stories primarily of the First and Second Age of Middle-earth that had never quite reached completion, even in draft form; some predate the writing of Lord of the Rings by decades but most come after, and the book includes some of Tolkien's last writings about Middle-earth. The stories are presented by his son Christopher who, presumably, selected the pieces that were nearest to completion and likeliest to be of interest to Middle-earth aficionados. The pieces are presented with introductions, footnotes, endnotes and editorial insertions, of which more anon. Several of the pieces are familiar, being expanded (albeit partial) versions of, e.g., the tales of Tuor and Túrin that were presented in brief form in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7332.The_Silmarillion" title="The Silmarillion by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Silmarillion</a>. Others provide glimpses of events leading up to, and that took place offstage during, the War of the Ring, beginning with the death of Isildur and the loss of the One Ring and continuing to include battles that were taking place "offstage" during the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/727800.The_Two_Towers__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___2_" title="The Two Towers (The Lord of the Rings, #2) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Two Towers</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/727810.The_Return_of_the_King__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___3_" title="The Return of the King (The Lord of the Rings, #3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Return of the King</a>. The book closes with essays about the Druedain (the Pukel-men), the Istari (the Wizards) and the Palantiri.<br /><br />Fascinating stuff, if you don't mind its incomplete and sometimes contradictory nature.<br /><br />Unfortunately I'm not sure if I can recommend the electronic version (which is what I read this time; previously, I was reading a print copy). The textual situation for many of the pieces is complex -- as mentioned above, there are footnotes and endnotes (some added by J.R.R. Tolkien during his drafting process and some added by Christopher Tolkien when assembling the pieces for publication) and editorial notes and changes of voice between the text and the commentary on the text. In the physical book this is handled by various combinations of font size and indentation; all of this formatting is lost in the electronic version, making it sometimes hard to distinguish the tales from the commentary. Footnotes and endnotes are better handled (on the Kindle you can hyperlink from the text to the associated note) but it's still less convenient than just flipping back and forth in a physical book. And finally, there were many more typos in the eBook than I'm comfortable with -- mostly things like missing spaces, hyphens dropped (or inappropriately retained) and the like. Nothing that rendered the text unreadable, but it still seemed to indicate a lack of editorial oversight on the eBook conversion process.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9197812322650052214" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review508612554">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_541817564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/541817564" />
    <a title="Chris Hall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9404007-chris-hall"><img alt="Chris Hall" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442649881p2/9404007.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/541817564?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Hall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Hall" href="/user/show/9404007-chris-hall">Chris Hall</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer541817564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17361514284465385812">This is a hard book to rate, because it's sort of like rating a compilation album of Led Zeppelin studio out-takes. If you love Led Zeppelin, you would undoubtedly want to listen to pretty much anything they did. On the other hand, objectively speaking, it's probably not their best work, and if you trust them as artists, you know why they left that material on the cutting room floor. And, indeed, this book is a collection of scrapings, random essays and bits of narrative illuminating obscure cor</span>
  <span id="freeText17361514284465385812" style="display:none">This is a hard book to rate, because it's sort of like rating a compilation album of Led Zeppelin studio out-takes. If you love Led Zeppelin, you would undoubtedly want to listen to pretty much anything they did. On the other hand, objectively speaking, it's probably not their best work, and if you trust them as artists, you know why they left that material on the cutting room floor. And, indeed, this book is a collection of scrapings, random essays and bits of narrative illuminating obscure corners of Middle Earth. <br /><br />I will say, though, that Christopher Tolkien deserves some credit for being a very conscientious offspring. Most children either end up hating their parents or thinking of them as basically foolish. JRR Tolkien's son, though is extraordinarily careful to give the exact providence and goes into excruciating detail as to the provenance of every piece of writing in Unfinished Tales. Never does he indulge himself in the slightest bit of irony at the expense of his father, or even hint at any frustration that, just maybe, he could have made his marginal annotations in more legible handwriting. The subtext of the father-son relationship, or lack thereof, might make this an interesting read... unless it actually doesn't. Really, for LotR/Middle Earth obsessives only. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17361514284465385812" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15363833958731833249" style="display:none">This is simply a moneymaking scheme. After the success of the Silmarillion, the Tolkien state has published all notes that were in a more or less readable state. This is the only one I bought (besides Chidren of Hurin, which probably has much in common with the bigger part of this book).<br /><br />I do not think Professor Tolkien would have liked to have these drafts and notes published. Many of them are even obsolete, as he built up and discarded elements in his mythic construct.<br /><br />There are some great storytelling moments (specially in the tales about Hurin and his children), but mostly it is not so interesting, except in an academic way, to see how Tolkien constructed and evolved his stories.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicky" href="/user/show/223837-nicky">Nicky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/223837-nicky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer232968900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13814477014815077375">This collection of Unfinished Tales is difficult to get to grips with, because Christopher Tolkien had the sense not to mess with them too much. He didn't correct inconsistencies or do too much to the material, and that's for the best: J.R.R.'s intent and the breadth of his world are best experienced this way, I think.<br/><br/>I don't think this is one for the casual reader, but for someone interested in Tolkien and his creation of a secondary world, and in the details of Middle-earth, it's a good one. E</span>
  <span id="freeText13814477014815077375" style="display:none">This collection of Unfinished Tales is difficult to get to grips with, because Christopher Tolkien had the sense not to mess with them too much. He didn't correct inconsistencies or do too much to the material, and that's for the best: J.R.R.'s intent and the breadth of his world are best experienced this way, I think.<br /><br />I don't think this is one for the casual reader, but for someone interested in Tolkien and his creation of a secondary world, and in the details of Middle-earth, it's a good one. Even more casual readers might like to dip into it for extra details about Gandalf, of course, but for the most part, if you didn't get into The Silmarillion, then don't bother with this.<br /><br />But if you've ever thought, if only Tolkien could've lived forever -- or at least much longer -- so that we could know more about Middle-earth, then yes, give it a try.<br /><br />Now if Christopher Tolkien would just let go of J.R.R.'s Arthurian poem, I'd be very grateful...</span>
  <a data-text-id="13814477014815077375" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2746317576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15894400303720272171">If you are not huge Tolkien fan or you haven't read<br/><i>Silmarillion</i> yet, I suggest you to to skip this book. For<br/>Tolkien fans <i>(as I am)</i>, who read <i>Silmarillion</i>, this will<br/>be nice and informative read. <div id="review_2026670359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2026670359" />
    <a title="Lydia Redwine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45581804-lydia-redwine"><img alt="Lydia Redwine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510521673p2/45581804.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2026670359?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lydia Redwine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lydia Redwine" href="/user/show/45581804-lydia-redwine">Lydia Redwine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45581804-lydia-redwine?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2026670359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17553729740657266076">Since I found some of these stories quite interesting and a couple others utterly boring, I've brought my rating to <b>4 stars.</b> I will say that it isn't a good idea to go into this book unless you are already an avid Tolkien fan. This book is a collection of unfinished pieces (I mean, the title?) from LOTR, The Hobbit, The Silmarillion and other like books. <br/><br/>If reading notes upon notes of what certain things could have meant etc. bores you to death, this book is not for you lol. I did find it all ve</span>
  <span id="freeText17553729740657266076" style="display:none">Since I found some of these stories quite interesting and a couple others utterly boring, I've brought my rating to <b>4 stars.</b> I will say that it isn't a good idea to go into this book unless you are already an avid Tolkien fan. This book is a collection of unfinished pieces (I mean, the title?) from LOTR, The Hobbit, The Silmarillion and other like books. <br /><br />If reading notes upon notes of what certain things could have meant etc. bores you to death, this book is not for you lol. I did find it all very interesting, however, since it gave me insight into Tolkien's writing process (I mean he started writing <i>The Silmarillion</i> during WWI surrounded by gramophones to distract himself from the war itself.) I'm also a huge geek for history in general whether that be history of the real world or of fictional worlds. <br /><br />The parts I enjoyed most were ones that directly filled gaps and/or answered questions arisen while reading <i>The</i> Hobbit and <i>Lord of the Rings</i>. Such as...Gandalf's reasons for helping Thorin Oakensheild defeat Smaug and take back his home and involving Bilbo in the whole affair directly from his own words. Further history on Galadriel is explored and because she is far more intriguing than she appears in <i>Lord of the Rings</i>, I loved it. Remember that rather confusing part in <i>Fellowship of the Ring</i> where she gets all creepy when Frodo offers her the ring but then says that she passed a test? Yeah, that's all explained among many other things. <br /><br />There are also included whole sections that speak of the hunt for the ring in LOTR but from the perspective of Sauron in a way and the Nazgul. Another part I heavily enjoyed was that of Haleth and her people who were mentioned in <i>The Silmarillion</i>. I mentioned in that review how much I loved and appreciated her character. More is revealed about their people and culture in this book which honestly bumped up the rating one star even if that section was brief. A few other stories were also very interesting to me. They were all like stories out of a collection of myths. <br /><br />Overall, I recommended this to anyone who loves <i>Lord of the Rings</i> and <i>The Hobbit</i> and those who have already read <i>The Silmarillion</i>. It is an excellent edition in terms of better understanding the world in history. Almost every so called "plot hole" that people talk about is explained in this book as well as in others. Tolkien, who was such a perfectionist when it came to writing, would not leave so many plot holes as some people think there to be. Of course, Tolkien's main work can be enjoyed without reading this. Also, I think Christopher Tolkien should be given a lot of credit for his likewise carefulness, abundance of notes, and respect for his father's work and the effect it has had on the world of literature. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17553729740657266076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14639981795058503796" style="display:none">09-10-19<br />Review to come on this... and man oh man, and boy oh boy is it going to be mixed. <br /><br />-----------------------------------------------<br />10-10-19 <br />Well. Hum. Hmm.. <br /><br />I am wavering with this book. It is important, first, to note that this book fills in certain gaps by including more tales that are featured within the Silmarillion. <br /><br />These unfinished tales include stories from the first second and third age of middle earth. It is imperative that anyone who reads this FIRST reads the Silmarillion, and before that have read the Hobbit and the Lord of the Rings. <br /><br />Now having gotten this all off my chest. <br /><br />I absolutely loved the story of the fall of Gondolin. But girl knows that she has to either fight the sea who has hold of him or she will be lost. And guess who wins THAT one. <br /><br />Sigh. <br /><br />Then. You get to galadriel and celeborn and man. Now it's getting boring. <br /><br />So the gist of the matter is this. This book is MUCH MUCH MORE denser than the Silmarillion. <br /><br />I really enjoyed the Silmarillion. And did not put it down. But this one. This one distressed me considering especially the children of hurin story. I really found it overwhelming and what not <br /><br />So. This book does indeed follow from the Silmarillion. So it is important to read after that book. But good luck to you all. Because this one was good in its way and yet. Oppressive, woeful and depressing in turns. <br /><br />I am now finished with Tolkien until I meet him again God willing In the fall of Gondolin. And thats it for me. Because, .... I THINK I have had enough now.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2323560670" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2323560670" />
    <a title="Ellen Trautner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29888746-ellen-trautner"><img alt="Ellen Trautner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437237818p2/29888746.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2323560670?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellen Trautner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellen Trautner" href="/user/show/29888746-ellen-trautner">Ellen Trautner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345357113" href="/book/show/92034.Unfinished_Tales_of_N_menor_and_Middle_earth">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29888746-ellen-trautner?shelf=tolkien">tolkien</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2323560670" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14570065216708717690">I can't believe I've never read this before! I would recommend this to anyone who's read the Silmarillion and is interested in more history of Middle-Earth. I say the Silmarillion because there's a lot of assumptions that the reader is familiar with the Valar, the Blessed Realm, and the general events of the First Age. You don't need to remember the details, but at least the basic narrative. Alternatively, if you just want more info on events of the Third Age, which is when the Lord of the Rings</span>
  <span id="freeText14570065216708717690" style="display:none">I can't believe I've never read this before! I would recommend this to anyone who's read the Silmarillion and is interested in more history of Middle-Earth. I say the Silmarillion because there's a lot of assumptions that the reader is familiar with the Valar, the Blessed Realm, and the general events of the First Age. You don't need to remember the details, but at least the basic narrative. Alternatively, if you just want more info on events of the Third Age, which is when the Lord of the Rings and the Hobbit take place, you could skip the first two sections and just read the third and I don't think you'd feel lost.<br /><br />This book is divided into three sections. Each one covers an age in Middle-Earth. The First Age only has two stories, the first of which is definitely "unfinished." It's about Tuor, an Elf-friend (and grandfather to Elrond, FYI) and the fall of Gondolin, the hidden Elvish kingdom. It's a great story that is told in brief in the Silmarillion. Here, it goes into much greater detail... but also stops before Tuor ever made it to Gondolin! Christopher Tolkien, J.R.R. Tolkien's son and editor of this book, only supplies what his father wrote. He adds footnotes and fragments that he can find, but it's definitely unfinished. As it was the first story in this book, I got worried that all of them would be like that: a structured narrative working to an exciting climax only to abruptly end. Luckily, that was only the case a few times.<br /><br />The only other story from the First Age is the tale of the children of Hurin, also told more briefly in the Silmarillion, but also recently it received its own standalone book treatment, so it hardly belongs in here. However, Christopher Tolkien offers lots of versions of different parts of the text, so you really learn a lot about the evolution of the story, which is focused on Turin (Tuor's cousin!) and his doom. It's a sad story.<br /><br />The second section is about the Second Age and focuses on Numenor, the island where come the Kings of Gondor and the Dunedain. The main story also ends somewhat abruptly and is sad in nature, but again, Christopher Tolkien outlines how it may have ended.<br /><br />There's also a lot of contradictory writings about Galadriel and Celeborn, and it seems Tolkien never made up his mind on what their history definitively was.<br /><br />The Third Age has a lot of interesting stories, including the history or Rohan and their friendship with Gondor, details of battles only briefly mentioned in the Lord of the Rings, the powers of the Nazgul, the five wizards and their origins, details about the palantirs, and more. These felt more complete, maybe because they weren't plot driven, but just interesting info.<br /><br />Loved it and will reread it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14570065216708717690" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1571841792" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1571841792" />
    <a title="E.F.B." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39244832-e-f-b"><img alt="E.F.B." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424876183p2/39244832.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1571841792?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="E.F.B." class="user" itemprop="url" name="E.F.B." href="/user/show/39244832-e-f-b">E.F.B.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780618154050" href="/book/show/357255.Unfinished_Tales_of_N_menor_and_Middle_earth">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=tolkien">tolkien</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=books-i-ll-read-again">books-i-ll-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39244832-e-f-b?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1571841792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7808641433872477672">Wow, that was a long one. It’s Tolkien though, so I was expecting that. 😉 What I wasn’t quite sure about was what was meant by these being “Unfinished Tales”. Turns out unfinished means exactly that. The stories featured here are ones that J.R.R. Tolkien never finished for one reason or another. Some are more complete than others, and Christopher Tolkien pieced together what he could from his father’s notes to try to figure out where the stories might have been going, and how they were connected</span>
  <span id="freeText7808641433872477672" style="display:none">Wow, that was a long one. It’s Tolkien though, so I was expecting that. 😉 What I wasn’t quite sure about was what was meant by these being “Unfinished Tales”. Turns out unfinished means exactly that. The stories featured here are ones that J.R.R. Tolkien never finished for one reason or another. Some are more complete than others, and Christopher Tolkien pieced together what he could from his father’s notes to try to figure out where the stories might have been going, and how they were connected to the wider world of Middle-earth and, but they still are just plain not finished.<br /><br />I appreciated that Christopher seemed just as sad as I was that some of the stories were never finished because quite of few of them were very interesting and enjoyable. To name a few, my favorites were definitely “Of Tuor and His Coming to Gondolin,” “A Description of the Island of Numenor,” “The History of Galadriel and Celeborn,” “The Quest for Erebor,” “The Hunt for the Ring,” and the majority of Part Four, especially, “The Druedain”. In spite of the lack of endings, I’m glad Christopher was able to piece together as much as he did because they really do add depth to his father’s (sub)creation. The man had an amazing imagination. <br /><br />I’m technically giving this book 4.5 stars just because there were sections of some stories that I skimmed because they weren’t quite interesting enough to hold my attention. With the exception of “Narn I Hin Hurin” which I’ve already read in its separate book form, “The Children of Hurin” and therefore didn’t feel a particular need to read again, there weren’t any stories that I skipped entirely, though. Each story held something of interest, it was just that some stories had parts that were over-descriptive in the scenery department, or sometimes were just things I already knew, so I skimmed them. <br /><br />One story, “Aldarion and Erendis” was a bit like watching a train wreck, only the train was the titular characters and the wreck was their relationship with each other. I just reached a point where all I could think was, “Okay, I get it, you’re both selfish jerks who have no business even considering marriage. Since I can’t reach through the page and smack sense into both of you, I must move on.” :P However, I do feel the story had value as a part of the history of Numenor and held some interesting glimpses at its culture, so at the very least, I’m glad it was included for that. People who enjoy angsty relationship drama would probably like it more than I did. :P<br /><br />Other than that one story, though, I can say I at least liked if not loved the rest of the stories and am very glad to have finally gotten around to reading Unfinished Tales. I’ve had it for nearly two years, it was just so thick I was a little intimidated by it. There was no need for intimidation, though. Just patience and a steady speed of reading. 😉<br /><br /><br /><b>Content Advisory:</b><br />I am usually as detailed as possible with the content advisories I include with my reviews, however, if you’re thinking about reading this book, more likely than not you are a steadfast fan of Tolkien and have read enough of his works to know his style. (If you haven’t, you should probably stop here and go read The Hobbit, LOTR, and The Silmarillion before attempting Unfinished Tales because several stories in it require at least some knowledge of those books to be fully appreciated.) Violent things occur in his books, and some of acts committed by evil creatures/characters are especially terrible, but Tolkien remains ever consistent in that he never describes the violence in a way that is gory or gross, though blood is briefly mentioned on rare occasion. The only story that some readers may want to warned about is “Nar I Hin Hurin” (aka The Children of Hurin.) If you haven’t read that story before, it is a tragedy through and through. Readers who are easily depressed may want to skip it entirely or wait to read it at a time when you are feeling emotionally able to handle the sadness. Be aware either way that two characters in that story commit suicide: One via throwing themselves into a river and one via sword. This is not any more graphic than any other violence in Tolkien’s works, but could still be disturbing to some nevertheless. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7808641433872477672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_55355526" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/55355526" />
    <a title="Kevis Hendrickson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1096765-kevis-hendrickson"><img alt="Kevis Hendrickson" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/55355526?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kevis Hendrickson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kevis Hendrickson" href="/user/show/1096765-kevis-hendrickson">Kevis Hendrickson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer55355526" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9991522266487112332">J.R.R. Tolkien's Unfinished Tales is a terrific book for diehard Tolkien fans, in particular, fans of The Lord of the Rings who have not yet read The Silmarillion. Ever wondered what were the exact events that caused Isildur to lose the One Ring? Or the origins of Wizards? Or what Middle-Earth was like during its First Age? Unfinished Tales helps to shed light on the complex creation of Middle-Earth and the many tales and legends that relate the events in its long and largely tumultuous history.</span>
  <span id="freeText9991522266487112332" style="display:none">J.R.R. Tolkien's Unfinished Tales is a terrific book for diehard Tolkien fans, in particular, fans of The Lord of the Rings who have not yet read The Silmarillion. Ever wondered what were the exact events that caused Isildur to lose the One Ring? Or the origins of Wizards? Or what Middle-Earth was like during its First Age? Unfinished Tales helps to shed light on the complex creation of Middle-Earth and the many tales and legends that relate the events in its long and largely tumultuous history.<br /><br />I found this book to be very interesting with a number of wonderful never before told tales from Tolkien's furiously hoarded safe box of writings such as "Of Tuor and His Coming to Gondolin", "The Disaster of The Gladden Fields" and my personal favorite "Aldarion and Erendis: The Mariner's Wife". Even in their sometimes incomplete state, the archaic nature of the tales contained in this book add to the mystique that Tolkien discovered a trove of ancient manuscripts in some dark and remote cave recounting a lost and forgotten age of our world rather than merely conjuring it up out of his vast and unfettered imagination.<br /><br />My only complaint about Unfinished Tales is that like the other history of Middle-Earth books, Tolkien's son and literary executor Christopher is too enamored of trivial events in his father's creation of Middle-Earth and seems too driven to point out every single nuance (and sometimes meaningless facts) about the many versions of the tales his father wrote before they came to their final, but incomplete forms. This makes for some rather unnecessarily confusing, if not, at times, dull reading.<br /><br />Even so, I would recommend this book to anyone who wants to learn more about how Tolkien created the world behind The Lord of the Rings and the many wondrous and previously unpublished tales that we could only guess had existed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9991522266487112332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer615187886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4946686965152801408">A fascinating look at many of the stories that did not make it into Professor Tolkien's primary works. This is probably one of my favorite books of this well-known mythology.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I think my favorite part of this book is the chapter concerning the history of Galadriel and Celeborn. Tolkien clearly had many different ideas for their origins, and it's utterly fascinating to see those ideas laid out. It also makes a person wonder what he ultimately would have laid down for them. <i>The Silmar</i></span></span>
  <span id="freeText4946686965152801408" style="display:none">A fascinating look at many of the stories that did not make it into Professor Tolkien's primary works. This is probably one of my favorite books of this well-known mythology.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I think my favorite part of this book is the chapter concerning the history of Galadriel and Celeborn. Tolkien clearly had many different ideas for their origins, and it's utterly fascinating to see those ideas laid out. It also makes a person wonder what he ultimately would have laid down for them. <i>The Silmarillion</i> gives us one version, but it seems that it was by no means meant to be the final word.<br /><br />Additionally, I greatly enjoyed the chapters that focused on Numenor and its inhabitants. The story of Aldarion and Erendis is so tragic, and the descriptions of their daughter Ancalimë remind me a great deal of Elizabeth I. Given how well-versed Tolkien was in history, I doubt that resemblance was coincidental. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Definitely worth the time of any fan of <i>Lord of the Rings</i> and its world.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16889723618403849980">I have so enjoyed finishing these Unfinished Tales with my chapter a day group. Tolkien was a great, and immensely nuanced storyteller, his son Christopher a devoted son and detailed story archiver, whose life work allowed us to see the depth of creativity and true craft his father put into all his tales. I’ve truly enjoyed the surface tale, as well as the the deeper tale behind its creation and evolution.</span>

<div id="review_3575006571" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3575006571" />
    <a title="Elentarri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19446286-elentarri"><img alt="Elentarri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450450712p2/19446286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3575006571?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elentarri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elentarri" href="/user/show/19446286-elentarri">Elentarri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008387952" href="/book/show/52033906-unfinished-tales">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19446286-elentarri?shelf=fantasy-and-sf">fantasy-and-sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3575006571" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14130311082279415084">******************POSSIBLE SPOILERS***********************<br/><br/><br/>Unfinished Tales of Numenor and Middle-earth is exactly that - a collection of tales from Tolkien's Middle-earth universe that didn't make it into the Silmarillion, the Hobbit or the Lord of the Rings. The book is split into the First, Second and Third Ages, and miscellaneous sundry material.<br/><br/>We have a more fleshed out narrative of Tuor's journey to find Gondolin, and the trials of Turin son of Hurin in the First Age, followed by a geograp</span>
  <span id="freeText14130311082279415084" style="display:none">******************POSSIBLE SPOILERS***********************<br /><br /><br />Unfinished Tales of Numenor and Middle-earth is exactly that - a collection of tales from Tolkien's Middle-earth universe that didn't make it into the Silmarillion, the Hobbit or the Lord of the Rings. The book is split into the First, Second and Third Ages, and miscellaneous sundry material.<br /><br />We have a more fleshed out narrative of Tuor's journey to find Gondolin, and the trials of Turin son of Hurin in the First Age, followed by a geography and history lesson on Numenor and the tragic love story of Erendis and Aldarion <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(Erendis is a bitch!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. There is additional information on Galadriel and Celeborn (Tolkien couldn't make up his mind!) and the ruin of Eregion <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(the elf who made all the magic rings ends up in Sauron's clutches) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />I found the sections involving the Third Age most interesting. These include a fuller narrative of what happened to Isildur on the Gladden Fields (and the interesting things Aragorn finds in Saruman's tower), several extended narratives on the politics and friendship between Gondor and Rohan, a "missing chapter" of the Battle of the Fords of Isen where Theodred was slain, and a hilarious extra "chapter" on Gandalf's quest to convince Thorin to take a hobbit with him to claim his Kingdom Under the Mountain. There is additional juicy information about Ringwraiths, Gollum, wizards, Seeing-Stones and a peculiar race of humans called the Druedain. <br /><br />It really is a pity that Tolkien didn't manage to add some of these "unfinished tales" into his novels, even as appendices. This book provides a selection of additional material for those who need to know more about Middle-Earth. However, I do suggest reading The Silmarillion, The Hobbit and The Lord of the Rings, before reading Unfinished Tales to get the most out of this book.<br /><br />NOTE: To celebrate its 40th anniversary, the first ever illustrated edition of this collection of tales has been published in October 2020.<br /><br />NOTE: Re-read. First copy of this book has been read and loved to death.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14130311082279415084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5389203267336120672" style="display:none">I've read quite a few parts of this previously, either due to individual curiosity about specific topics (such as the Quest of Erebor, Istari, Palantiri) or as part of other works (Narn i Hin Hurin – most of which is incorporated in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3141295.The_Children_of_Hurin_The_Silmarillion_The_Hobbit_The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Children of Hurin/The Silmarillion/The Hobbit/The Lord of the Rings by J.R.R. Already a big fan of Tolkien, as a whole I quite enjoyed the collection, especially since Christopher Tolkien's notes and analysis are kept at a minimum compared when compared with the various volumes of HoME.<br /><br />Of the tales I had not read previously, I most enjoyed that of Aldarion and Erendis, as well as brief story of the Druedain, perhaps because I knew the least about them already.<br /><br />Highly recommended for anyone who has already read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5907.The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hobbit</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_" title="The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Silmarillion</a>.</span>
